In reading the NY Daily News article, she is practically ordained by the local Democratic Right:

Quote
These early endorsements are intended to send a message that the Democratic establishment is lining up behind Simotas, just in case anyone is thinking of challenging her. To my knowledge, no other Democrat has yet announced his or her intention to run.

There is nothing organic about Simotas' candidacy.  You want somebody that represents you, not someone being groomed by the likes of Quinn, Gianaris and Vallone to continue an unremarkable legacy of representation.

She has a law degree and she lives in Astoria.  She was appointed to Community Board 1.  That's it.  Anyone can say they support gay rights or speak on other issues that is fashionable to get elected, but not many people put themselves out there.  And she has not.

Her candidacy reflects a broken system with hapless voters lulled into the mindset they actually have viable candidate choices in this community.  At least her well-connected supporters won't have to do a lot of legwork in getting her elected.

Title: Re: Early LGBT support for Simotas in Astoria
Post by: Equal in Astoria on March 18, 2010, 01:43:25 PM
I don’t know why you posted this twice Steve Crawford, but I am responding on both threads so in case you are only checking one.

I can’t believe anyone can sincerely state that Simotas would have more support from the gay community than Jeremiah Frei-Pearson! Few if any Astorians who are politically active in the marriage equality movement or who were involved in the local movement to pressure George Onorato have heard of Simotas. Simotas may have secured approval from prominent gay politicians but I have yet to hear any praise from any actual Astorians involved in LGBT issues.

All we know about Simotas now is that she has loyally served Mike Gianaris and the Queens Democratic party, but we know little to nothing about her community involvement and have yet to see if she has gone to the streets to stand up for the rights of any group, let alone the LGBT community.

Frei-Pearson on the other hand has been an inspirational and dependable ally to the LGBT community and the marriage equality movement. It is absurd to accuse him of not being involved. I can only assume that the person posting that is ignorant of Astoria LGBT issues or is intentionally lying.

Frei-Pearson has put in more time than most LGBT people on marriage equality! It is an issue near and dear to both he and his wife, both of whom could be seen regularly last summer handing out fliers on street corners, attending rallies, and at many meetings. Let me emphasize the point that Frei-Pearson has not just stood up in front of crowds of thousands arguing for marriage equality. He is not one of those “gay friendly” politicians who just shows up at the right PR moments. Frei-Pearson has done the truly thankless, gritty, at times personally risky task, time and time again of standing on the street asking strangers to support marriage equality and to become more active in their government. If there were more straight people like Frei-Pearson, there would no longer be “gay issues” because LGBT people would have full equality and complete social acceptance.

Both Simotas and Frei- Pearson are pro marriage equality and this is a blessing for the LGBT community so now we need to see where they stand on all the OTHER issues. Challenge Frei-Pearson on a real issue in play but for God’s sake, don’t question his incredible service to the LGBT community. After all the time and work he has put in standing along side us, after all the times he has put himself out there to publically defend us, it is offensive to say that he isn’t involved in “any real community issues”… unless of course, you don’t think protecting the relationships and families of a growing number of Astorians with marriage equality is a “real” community issue. I hope the rumors of Frei-Pearson running are true. We don’t need more politicians whose records show consistent service to a party, we need more politicians whose records show them consistently standing for what is right.

Title: Jeremiah Frei-Pearson at DFNYC
Post by: mangopaco on April 07, 2010, 11:16:57 PM
I went to the DFNYC candidate forum tonight to hear both Assembly candidates speak.  I arrived a few minutes late and caught what seemed like the second half of Jeremiah Frei-Pearson (http://jeremiahfp.org/)'s opening.  I was surprised to learn that Simotas didn't show up.  Having clicked on the link earlier, I knew she was unconfirmed, but seriously? 

In a local election that is decided by less than 10,000 voters, you would think that the candidates are looking for as much public face time as they can get.  As someone said on the earlier Simotas thread (http://www.astorians.com/community/index.php?topic=17670.15), she's going to have to do more than ask for money on her website to get any votes (http://www.aravellasimotas.com (http://www.aravellasimotas.com)).

The crowd at the DFNYC event was well-informed and asked some pretty good questions of Frei-Pearson.  His campaign seems to revolve around reforming Albany.  I particularly liked the idea of implementing term limits in our State government.  As he said, the seat belongs to the people, and no one should be able to sit in one for forty years.  He also talked about Campaign Finance reform as another way of ensuring more fair elections.

I have to say, I liked his ideas but also his honesty.  There were some suggestions from the crowd - like on residential parking permits - where he didn't seem completely committed to endorsing the idea, but he would say that he liked the idea, would look into it, and have a better answer later.  It's obvious he's not trying to make himself out to be a know-it-all savior type.  He's real, willing to take input from the constituents and have a conversation about it, and honest about his thought process.

This is the first time I've seen Frei-Pearson in a forum/debate (is it a debate if the other person doesn't show up?) and I was really impressed with him.  I felt like he really connected.

I'm looking forward to hearing more from him but also from Simotas.  I want to hear what she stands for - aside from just asking for money.

Title: Re: Jeremiah Frei-Pearson at DFNYC
Post by: mcdirk on April 08, 2010, 10:55:34 AM
Quote from: mangopaco on April 07, 2010, 11:16:57 PM
The crowd at the DFNYC event was well-informed and asked some pretty good questions of Frei-Pearson.  His campaign seems to revolve around reforming Albany.  I particularly liked the idea of implementing term limits in our State government.  As he said, the seat belongs to the people, and no one should be able to sit in one for forty years.  He also talked about Campaign Finance reform as another way of ensuring more fair elections.

I think term limits could be a positive thing, though I was opposed to them at the city level initially.  I do think they brought new blood and vibrancy to the City Council.  My only fear with term limits is it makes candidates more likely to be looking for their next office and liable to grand-stand instead of deliver results, though turnover has been positive, on the whole, at the city level.  More important, in my opinion, than term limits are campaign finance reform and redistricting reform - I don't think we'll see a lot of change until we see some movement on those two issues.

Title: Re: JFP at DFNYC
Post by: mcdirk on April 08, 2010, 11:44:53 AM
Quote from: mangopaco on April 08, 2010, 11:13:17 AM
I agree that it's early, but I guess the "season" started early this year anyway - those two Democratic Clubs endorsed her back in January or February.  I hope they have more of these as well.  I do want to be able to compare and contrast the two candidates.

There were no questions on education.  I'll take the fault on that one, I'm a public school teacher, and didn't even think to ask about a number of things.  I'll have to email the campaign or find out when the next forum is.

I think the race is starting to heat up, a bit earlier than usual - but then it's an open seat, which doesn't happen that often, so there is a lot of excitement.  County Regular Democratic Clubs endorse once the District Leaders have had a chance to assess the field,  the official Queens County Democratic Organization designation usually takes place in late May prior to petitioning. 

Unions are also starting to talk with candidates and advocacy groups (League of Conservation Voters, Planned Parenthood, NARAL, League of Humane Voters, etc.) are all starting to get questionnaires out, though they don't all endorse before petitioning (June and the beginning of July).
Title: Re: Early LGBT support for Simotas in Astoria
Post by: mcdirk on April 08, 2010, 11:51:39 AM
I don't think Aravella is a one issue candidate.  She's been a member of Community Board 1 for over 8 years and has been active with UCCA, the largest civic association in Astoria for a long time as well.  She's a lifelong resident of Astoria, over 31 years and she worked on the campaigns of the Vallones and Mike Gianaris.  I know she's been particularly involved in women's issues, immigration (she was born in Zimbabwe herself and is an immigrant) and has worked on Greek concerns for many years.  I'm very impressed with her (and in the interests of full disclosure, have endorsed her - I serve as the President of the Powhatan Regular Democratic Club which is behind her and my boss, Congresswoman Carolyn Maloney, is officially endorsing her on Saturday).

That all being said, I am a huge fan of Jeremiah as well (we're both congregants at Trinity Lutheran Church and he's also a member of Powhatan, and has been an incredible advocate on marriage equality).  He's truly one of the best people I know and would also be an outstanding Assemblymember.

I'm sure they'll be updating the website soon - I was surprised that the splashpage is only the donation page, but that happens with campaigns sometimes - they roll out the website in pieces.

Title: Re: Jeremiah Frei-Pearson at DFNYC
Post by: costa01 on April 08, 2010, 08:27:18 PM
I feel compelled to comment here on last night's forum since my name is attached to the DFNYC linkup here in Astoria.  As many of the people on this blog have seen, I have been posting DFNYC events here for almost 3 years.  I wear a lot of hats here in Astoria, DFNYC co-host as one of them.  I love this organization and have worked hard for the ideals that they stand for.  Last night, I was not in attendance because I was attending the rehearsal class for my son's baptism coming up.

Last night's forum was not promoted accurately.  Jeremiah knew very well that Aravella Simotas was not attending the forum weeks in advance.  His promotion of this event as a "forum" when he knew all too well that this was not going to be a forum is disappointing.  This was a "meet and greet" for Jeremiah Frei-Pearson.  It should have been promoted that way. It should have been in a non-publicly funded space that was appropriate for a meet and greet and not the Greater Astoria Historical Society.  There would have been nothing wrong with him being honest about the event.  People would have come to hear him speak!! There would be no shame in that.

So instead, he stands up and smacks an opponent for not being somewhere that he knew she wasn't going to be.  That isn't what DFNYC is all about.  A good government group like DFNYC deserves better.  The fact that he attached my name to an email promoting the event that was misleading is frustrating for me personally, but I am a big boy I'll survive  :-).  I am more disappointed that the people in attendance didn't get what they came in expecting and everyone looks silly. 

I will be strongly supporting Aravella Simotas for this seat because I think she can do the better job and bring back to Astoria the resources that we need. Jeremiah is a nice guy who I respect both personally and professionally and I have worked with him to do some good things.   But on this one, he made a mistake that disappoints me.  And he will not be the person I will be supporting for Assembly.

Found something informative, would like to see more bio and resumes of the candidates.
From employer bio -

Quote

A life-long New Yorker, Aravella Simotas received her bachelor of arts degree, summa cum laude, from Fordham University in 1999 and her juris doctor degree from Fordham University School of Law in 2002. During law school, Ms. Simotas served as the managing editor of the Fordham Environmental Law Journal. She also worked as a district representative to the former Speaker of the New York City Council. An active community member, she has served on the Queens Community Board 1 since her May 2002 appointment by the Borough President.


Before joining Bickel & Brewer, Ms. Simotas clerked for Senior Judge Nicholas Tsoucalas and Judge Timothy C. Stanceu at the U.S. Court of International Trade (“CIT”). At the CIT, she focused on U.S. international trade law disputes between the United States and private parties. Such matters involved complex issues of administrative law. In addition, Ms. Simotas gained experience in a variety of civil and criminal matters during designation sittings at the Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit and the U.S. District Court for the Southern District of New York.

Ms. Simotas is admitted to practice in New York, New Jersey, the U.S. District Courts for the Southern District and Eastern District of New York, and the CIT.

Title: Discussion: Jeremiah Frei Pearson and Costas email controversy
Post by: sting55 on April 10, 2010, 11:25:23 AM
So here is the situation. Jeremiah Frei Pearson sent out this email below to progressive groups throughout NYC:

Dear Astoria Linkup Friends,
 
I apologize for the late notice, but I'm very excited about this month's linkup.  DFNYC and the Astoria Historical Society have put together a candidate forum for the 36th Assembly District.  The linkup/forum is TONIGHT (Wednesday) at 7:00 at the Astoria Historical Society (35-20 Broadway, 4th Floor).  This is a joint linkup, so we will be joined by folks from around the city and from our community. 
 
The forum will be moderated by Dan Miner, the Chair of the New York City Sierra Club.  All candidates have been invited and every effort has been made to accomodate schedules.  As best we can tell, there is no legitimate campaign conflict that should prevent any candidate from attending.  I will definitely be there and I'm looking forward to seeing all of you there as well.
 
Full disclosure:  I am a candidate in this race. The other announced candidate is Aravella Simotas.  I encourage you all to come with your questions and to hear from us both before you make your decision.
 
Best,
Jeremiah & Costa

Costa, a well known community activist and major progressive figure in NYC had this responce:

I feel compelled to comment here on last night's forum since my name is attached to the DFNYC linkup here in Astoria.  As many of the people on this blog have seen, I have been posting DFNYC events here for almost 3 years.  I wear a lot of hats here in Astoria, DFNYC co-host as one of them.  I love this organization and have worked hard for the ideals that they stand for.  Last night, I was not in attendance because I was attending the rehearsal class for my son's baptism coming up.

Last night's forum was not promoted accurately.  Jeremiah knew very well that Aravella Simotas was not attending the forum weeks in advance.  His promotion of this event as a "forum" when he knew all too well that this was not going to be a forum is disappointing.  This was a "meet and greet" for Jeremiah Frei-Pearson.  It should have been promoted that way. It should have been in a non-publicly funded space that was appropriate for a meet and greet and not the Greater Astoria Historical Society.  There would have been nothing wrong with him being honest about the event.  People would have come to hear him speak!! There would be no shame in that.

So instead, he stands up and smacks an opponent for not being somewhere that he knew she wasn't going to be.  That isn't what DFNYC is all about.  A good government group like DFNYC deserves better.  The fact that he attached my name to an email promoting the event that was misleading is frustrating for me personally, but I am a big boy I'll survive  .  I am more disappointed that the people in attendance didn't get what they came in expecting and everyone looks silly. 

I will be strongly supporting Aravella Simotas for this seat because I think she can do the better job and bring back to Astoria the resources that we need. Jeremiah is a nice guy who I respect both personally and professionally and I have worked with him to do some good things.   But on this one, he made a mistake that disappoints me.  And he will not be the person I will be supporting for Assembly. 

Waiting for Jeremiah to let us know what his side of the story is on this emerging controversy.

Title: Re: Jeremiah Frei-Pearson at DFNYC
Post by: deaghaidh on April 11, 2010, 10:05:13 AM
I consider myself friendly with both Jeremiah and Aravella.  Jeremiah goes to Trinity with my friend Dirk, and I was part of the advisory committee that ran Western Queens for Marriage Equality. Aravella and I met through some common friends on Community Board 1 and some common friends through the Helenic Society.  She also exchanges recipes with me often.

On personal levels I get along with both and think they are genuinely nice people.  There are many of us who have to maneuver our way through this election because of the insular nature of a small community like Astoria.

I have no desire to speak against either candidate.  I have been helped last year by the Aravella/Gianaris camp on some unemployment insurance troubles--and am extremely grateful for the diligence in helping me deal with a very bad employer separation situation.  I also respect highly Mike Gianaris additionally because of his constant support for LGBT issues, and the change he has brought to the political spectrum here in Astoria.  Further, I respect Daniel Dromm and Jimmy Van Bramer, both personal friends and leaders of the LGBT community that have integrity and do not just go with the political machine--but actually stand for what they believe.  I am surprised at the dismissal of their endorsement by my friends who support Jeremiah, and accusations tantamount to calling the same leaders political hacks.  Jimmy has been integral in molding the Queens library system to the flagship that it is now, and he has been actively seeking office for many years, and has dedicated himself to our LGBT causes.  Daniel Dromm has been an activist well into the 80s and served our Education system and the UFT when our County leaders did not.  He lead a campaign against the County candidate this past year and won. Neither of these two are county "Yes" Men.

Their endorsement speaks words to me about Aravella and the work she has done with Community Board 1 and the UACC.  And if you know anything about Rose Marie and the UACC, you know that they are a civic organization that does not cow-tow to political leaders.

I like Jeremiah, and I have worked with him on marriage equality.  He was an active advocate, like so many of us; and he was a leader in 2009, like so many of us that joined the Coalition that is Western Queens for Marriage Equality.

I am fortunate to know both of the candidates, and grateful that both are on the right page with the issues that mean the most to me.  I know that whoever wins, this district will be a vote for YES on marriage equality.

However, given my experience and friendship with both, the work of Aravella on Community Board 1 and the UACC, and the endorsements of leaders I respect, and the help I've received from the Aravella/Gianaris camp, I am going to endorse and support Aravella Simotas.

Title: Re: Jeremiah Frei-Pearson at DFNYC
Post by: mjmurphy on April 11, 2010, 10:44:13 PM
I have not participated in this web forum before but I'm a resident of Astoria and a vocal supporter of Jeremiah's candidacy. I am not a paid spokesman for his campaign but I wanted to be clear about where I stand on this race before I said my piece. I cannot respond to any of the accusations--many unsubstantiated--made on this forum. I can only speak for myself and why I support Jeremiah.

Jeremiah Frei-Pearson has the courage and integrity to be a true leader in a time when our government in New York is known more for scandal and corruption. He has a strong public record of fighting for the little guy. He works as an attorney for Children's Rights, where he helps get children out of broken foster systems into caring, safe, and healthy homes. He's well known in Astoria as part of the legal team who won a $63 million dollar settlement from ConEd to compensate the victims of the 2006 Queens Blackout and fund neighborhood Greening projects to improve the quality of life in our communities. Jeremiah rallied with the gay and lesbian community to fight for marriage rights and helped found Western Queens for Marriage Equality. He works with the Long Island City Alliance to keep poorly-planned development from disfiguring our neighborhoods.

It's been mentioned on this forum several times that Jeremiah's opponent is a lifelong resident of Astoria. Jeremiah may not have lived in Astoria his entire life but in a community as rich with immigrants as ours, I don't feel being a lifelong resident is necessary to hold public office. Neither does the law, which only requires 5 years of State residence and 12 months in the District to run for the Assembly. Jeremiah more than meets both qualifications. Many of us have moved here from somewhere else but few have worked as hard for our communities as Jeremiah. His candidacy has been met with enthusiastic support by many residents--myself obviously included.

I have no desire to speak against Jeremiah's opponent in this race. She has the endorsement of many worthy figures in our community. But it takes more than endorsements to win the support of this Astorian. Our government is making headlines for scandal practically every week and we need candidates with a strong public record of working for our communities, a history of fighting when the odds are tough, and a willingness to stand up to authority when necessary. Jeremiah Frei-Pearson has all of those qualities in abundance and I am proud to support him.

[
Rather than cut spending, state legislators are seeking ways to raise taxes and fees and by borrowing money in huge amounts, the state Conservative Party charged in a release.

“The budget deficit will not be closed by: raising taxes and fees, by borrowing $6 billion, by fiscal gimmicks, using money intended for specific needs, and certainly not with unrealistic projections of income—for example the income from increased gambling outlets,” the release said. ]



I hope Aravella and Jeremiah will be supporting a number of Albany reforms :

http://www.legislativegazette.com/Articles-c-2010-03-15-66050.113122_Bill_would_drastically_change_member_item_distribution.html

http://www.citizensunion.org

Restore the public’s trust.
• Ensure that ethic, lobbying and campaign finance watchdogs are independent and powerful.
• End the practice of legislators drawing their own district lines.

• Provide fairness in allocating legislative resources, including distributions of “member items.”
• Reform the legislature's rules to increase transparency, accountability, and public input.
• Ban the personal use of campaign contributions.

Reform the state’s finances.

• Close obsolete public authorities.
• Establish an independent fiscal watchdog.
• Open up the government’s budget books and put them on-line.
Curb the power of special interests
• End “pay to play” for lobbyists and seekers – and receivers – of government contracts.
• Require the public disclosure of “independent” campaign contributions and close loopholes.
• Bolster the role of small donors in the campaign finance system.
• Restrict transfers from parties and legislative political committees to individual candidates
• Dramatically reduce the allowable size of campaign contributions.


In other local news, see also City Affairs - LuLu watch

http://www.citizensunion.org/site_res_view_folder.aspx?

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: deaghaidh on April 22, 2010, 03:50:56 AM
I attended the Simotas opening event.  It was not as showy as JFP's looks like it will be, but it was open to the public, and my email invitation said to share it with anyone who would be interested, and I did.  It was very well attended, and Simotas made Pistacchio herself.  I do not think they spent a lot of $$ on the event, despite her financials saying she raised a lot of money by that point, but as such, I'm more inclined to support her financially because it wasn't that extravagant.

Carolyn Maloney and Joe Crowley was there, as were a lot of electeds, and Mustafah who I believe was a potential candidate, but had chosen to support her instead.  Our presumed Senator-elect Gianaris was also there.  There were kids and adults. 

Gianaris is someone who has brought progressive politics to the area, and who did not need goading by WQfME to vote the right way in the Assembly.  He is not corrupt, and has voted right on all of the LGBT issues, and I would assume well acquainted with JFP.  In fact I know many in JFP's camp who claim to support and like Gianaris.  I'm not sure how that is going to play out, and am curious if the altruism of JFP will allow him to endorse a progressive Senator who has endorsed someone else.  In the world of politics alone, usually it's a "I'll do you if you do me".  We know where Gianaris stands, so it will be curious, if JFP would endorse him for who he is and his record, or not because no endorsement back.  Similarly, that will go for Carolyn Maloney. 

Maloney's opponent appears to be being run by the bankers--a lot of wall street money, and IMHO because of the Credit Card restriction act that she authored and got passed--which I'm extremely grateful to her because it directly effected me.  I am curious who JFP will endorse since, Carolyn too has endorsed Aravella.  Carolyn--a US Congresswman who I think has done a very good job representing me--not just a member of the political machine. 

When it comes to petitioning, it is most likely the case that Maloney, Gianaris, and Simotas will be on the same petition...will JFP partner with Rushma, or will he be on the petition by himself?

I do not know the answers, but these are questions I feel should be asked.

To try and show some side of unbiased response - I am not fully sure that JFP's move into the district was conscious or not.  I do know he got married to a wonderful woman and actress, and as a result moved from one home that I believe was in Markey's district, to what I believe is a home in Gianaris' district.  With the odd interweaving of the district, I cannot say it is more than coincidental.  I AM curious to know that if he had remained in Markey's district if he would have primaried her, especially since she DID NOT vote the right way on marriage equality.  Personally, I wish he would have stayed in her district and done just that, even though again he would be running against the alleged and so-called party machine. 

I am curious if he has answers to some of the other questions Sting is asking.  His voting record is important as an elected official because it shows how engaged one is in the process, as well as, if they are vocal about a person like Obama, if they backed it with a vote.  I am not sure, but I would guess that anyone who chooses to run for a public office agrees to disclose their voting record, though it is pure speculation.  I know that in phonebanking, if one voted in an election, your name appears on the list of dems who voted.  Additionally, I've heard people mention prime voters--those who've voted often and in primaries... so perhaps all the records are public to some extent.

I can't speak against JFP on this, he's a good guy and a friend, as is his wife Karla.  And I join Dirk and them at Trinity.  I have no personal beef with him at all, and any concerns regarding this run I've had, I've openly expressed to him. 

I am an advocate of speaking pro-somoene vs. against someone.  I am supporting Aravella because of her work with civic organizations like UACC, and for her work on CB1.  I've already said that I respect the electeds that came out in the LGBT community, none of which are party-machine folks.  They have integrity, and I weighing heaviest are Dromm and Van Bramer who I highly respect, and have seen stand against the County machine.  I do not think they would endorse blindly or because they were told to just do that.  That's not my experience with them. 

Well, anyway, I'll be off to Minneapolis now.  Back on Saturday-- I hope no one verbally kills anyone whilst I'm gone.
Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: sting55 on April 22, 2010, 12:43:58 PM
Here is a story in todays Astoria Times.


Simotas leads money race by 4-to-1 margin


By Nathan Duke
Thursday, April 22, 2010 11:13 AM EDT

 
Jeremiah Frei-Pearson (l.) and Aravella Simotas are both running for state Assemblyman Michael Gianaris' seat this fall.
Two young Democrats who work as Manhattan attorneys will face off this fall in the race to replace Michael Gianaris (D-Astoria) as the state assembly member for Astoria.

Aravella Simotas, a Manhattan litigator and Community Board 1 member, has already been endorsed by a number of Queens elected officials, such as U.S. Reps. Carolyn Maloney (D-Astoria) and Joseph Crowley (D-Jackson Heights), Gianaris, former City Council Speaker Peter Vallone Sr., Council Speaker Christine Quinn (D-Manhattan) and Councilmen Peter Vallone Jr. (D-Astoria), Daniel Dromm (D-Jackson Heights) and Jimmy Van Bramer (D-Sunnyside).

Jeremiah Frei-Pearson, who works as a civil and children’s rights attorney in Manhattan, is active in a number of civic groups, such as Western Queens Power for the People, Democracy for New York City, Coalition for a Better Astoria and the Long Island City Alliance.

Simotas has raised $49,490, according to state campaign finance records, while Frei-Pearson currently has $11,380.

Gianaris has raised nearly $100,000 in his bid for state Sen. George Onorato’s (D-Astoria) seat after the senator announced earlier this year that he would retire. He currently faces no opponents.

Simotas kicked off her campaign April 10 at Astoria’s Taminent Club, drawing several hundred people of varying ages.

“It’s great that the younger generation is getting involved in politics and government,” Simotas said. “A new generation of leadership is coming through in Astoria.”

Frei-Pearson said he would make his campaign official during a concert at Astoria’s Athens Square Park at 6 p.m. April 26.

“Albany is very dysfunctional,” he said. “My opponent is picked by Albany leaders, but she’s not going to fundamentally change the system.”

Simotas said she would focus on funding and improvements for public schools, environmental issues and expanding hospital space and health clinics in western Queens. Frei-Pearson said term limits and campaign finance reform were key issues as well as health care access, school overcrowding and the economy.

Mike Murphy, campaign spokesman for Simotas, criticized Frei-Pearson for his role in Western Queens Power for the People, which sued Con Edison for the 10-day blackout in July 2006. Frei-Pearson was one of two attorneys who worked with the group.

Power for the People reached a $7.9 million settlement in 2008 with the utility for planting trees and other green initiatives in western Queens. But some community leaders, including Gianaris, said the group should not have settled on the community’s behalf.

“The people of Astoria know they can trust Aravella Simotas,” Murphy said. “She’s a lifelong resident who understands the needs of the community and will fight for expanded access for health care and better schools. That’s why she’s endorsed by all the leaders we can trust. He’s already betrayed our community by selling them out to Con Edison after we suffered through the blackout.”

Frei-Pearson downplayed a recent message posted by Astoria district leader Costa Constantinides, with whom he runs Astoria’s Democracy for New York City meetings, on the community Web site astorians.com.

In the message, Constantinides said he believed Frei-Pearson had not promoted a DFNYC forum “accurately” by mentioning that his opponent would attend. Constantinides wrote he was frustrated his name was attached to an e-mail promoting the event and that Frei-Pearson knew Simotas would not be in attendance.

“I think there are important issues facing the community, so this is political nonsense,” said Frei-Pearson.

Constantinides did not want to comment on the matter, but both he and Frei-Pearson said they have worked together through DFNYC for years. However, Constantinides has thrown his support behind Simotas.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: sting55 on April 24, 2010, 06:14:40 PM
The Con Edison deal is a real issue. BTW, calling it a lawsuit is kinda not correct.

Read this excerpt from the Public Service Commisions own press release: http://www3.dps.state.ny.us/pscweb/WebFileRoom.nsf/Web/C0CAEF47EA0A107C852574880067659B/$File/pr08080.pdf?OpenElement

Disallowance of Repair Costs

The settlement contains two basic monetary provisions which were offered by Con
Edison in exchange for the termination of the prudence investigation instituted by the
Commission in April 2007. The first is the disallowance of $40 million of plant costs and $6
million of accrued carrying charges incurred by Con Edison to replace and repair electricity
delivery facilities in the Long Island City network associated with the July 2006 power outages.
The second is Con Edison’s provision of $17 million in community-benefit funds dedicated to
the community directly affected by the 2006 Queens power outage.

So, the "settlement" was actually proposed by Con Edison. Read it clearly, there was no "lawsuit" that brought Con Edison to their knees. This is the NYS Public Service Commissions own press release. This "deal" was proposed by Con Edison.

And it was done, and pay close attention here, " in exchange for the termination of the prudence investigation instituted by the Commission in April 2007."

So, Con Edison proposed giving everyone $100 in credits on their bill (zero cash) and giving a not-for-profit 17M to plant trees.

We, the citizens, agreed to "terminate" an "investigation" as to why the blackout actually occured and forgoe any penalties.

And, some very in-experienced press hungry activists formed a brand new group, Western Queens Power Brokers, and signed on to this horrible crime.

And now, Jeremiah is running with this "lawsuit" (which it was not) as one of his main platforms.

So, lets talk on the merits here about maybe the most single important thing to hit this community in a whole bunch of years. Thanks.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: deaghaidh on April 30, 2010, 10:28:30 AM
I do not agree with the personal attacks on either side, or at individuals specifically. 

I am curious why JFP's camp (which I know you're part of MJM since I know you personally), has not responded to stings accusations.  I do not feel it is my place to inflame the situation, but I am curious why there has been no clarification.  If the accusations are truly without merit, they should be easily defended against. 

So rather than this being about JFP or AS, this has turned more into a supporter-vs-supporter attack session that is not helpful.

1. It is fact that JFP sent an email inviting folks to a debate between him and AS and "signed" Costa's name in the email.  Costa has posted on the board a rather direct comment addressing this, confirming that it was done, and saying that the premise of "debate" was incorrect and that JFP knew that AS would not be able to attend well in advance, despite the letter leading folks on to the contrary.  As of date, no response has been posted explaining this from JFP or a rep.

2. Sting alleges that JFP has moved into the district 5 or 6 months ago with the sole intent to run for the Assembly.  I am not sure how one could prove or disprove intention, but I think if JFP DID move into the district he should own up to it.  It is my understanding, as a friend of his, that he had moved in that time period, related to his wedding.  I cannot confirm or deny any special intent on why he moved to where he did within Astoria.  I can confirm that our Assembly district lines are very oddly shaped, that I recently moved, and that it took me some time to figure out which Assembly District I live in.  Some clarification from JFP would be helpful.

3. Sting alleges that JFP did not vote in some important elections and primaries.  JFP has not refuted this on the board.  Those who speak against sting's allegations focus more on why the voting record is public.  I would be curious why he did not vote in the presidential primary, especially with his public statements of support for Obama. 

4. I have raised concern that JFP sent an email blast about "lulu"s claiming that none of the folks in Albany deserved them, despite the good work that our Assembly did, especially Mike Gianaris (emphasis is mine).  He said in his blast that none of them deserved a bonus.  I have to disagree, as I think Mike Gianaris has done an excellent job as an Assemblyman, bringing Astoria from Onorato-style politics to a mainline democratic politics--at a time when it was not yet popular in this constituency.  He voted the right way on many issues in the past, but most notably he voted FOR marriage equality both times it came up last year.  He DID a good job, does a good job, and I believe will do an even better job as our Senator.  Blanket statements like JFP made in his blast are concerning.   I know that several folks on JFP's camp have expressed that they intend to support Gianaris personally and JFP personally.  I am curious if JFP is going to do the same by endorsing Gianaris even though he knows the endorsement is not returned.  My challenge is that the endorsement is altruistic and not a political ploy...will he endorse our presumed democratic Senatorial candidate before the primary?  Similarly, will he endorse Maloney who has also endorsed AS?  I am a big fan of Gianaris and Maloney (in addition to Simotas), and it is of interest that any Assembly candidate saying they're doing this out of good-will support those who have done great things for us already.

5. I am curious about petitioning.  It is very likely that ballot petitions will be including Maloney, Gianaris, and Simotas on one petition.  Will JFP be petitioning with opponents to Maloney and Gianaris?  Or will he have a petition that is only his, aware that anyone who signs the M/G/S petition would not be able to sign his and vice versa? 

6. Maloney took a major stand against the Credit Card businesses.  She helped pass one of the most important Acts protecting citizens from exploitation by the same.  As a result she has a Wall St. well-financed opponent challenging her.  What is JFP's opinion on this and will he stand by Maloney?

7. Sting has raised allegations regarding the ConEd settlement, offering documentation that JFP's website refers to it in a different manner than the official press release.  Though it is often semantics, several folks who were on the fence on this issue also admitted to this.  I've still not seen any explanation refuting the allegations of Sting other than attacks on his tone and presentation.  I was not part of either side on this issue, though I do see the merit in questioning the settlement, as $100 electric credit does seem like a hollow gesture, and I think there are more important issues facing Astoria than trees, especially if we may still have remaining problems that could cause another black-out.  Similarly related, a newspaper asked AS her opinion on the settlement, and she spoke positively of it but mentioned that Mt. Sinai could use some of that money to become a better facility in the area.  I received an email from JFPs camp accusing her of hijacking "his win".  I rolled my eyes, as it appeared they were clearly reading into the situation--and it made them appear like they were trying to be victims.  (That was early on in the campaign, and probably what initially led me to be a Simotas supporter, as I do not like feigned sensationalized victimization).

8. Several folks including the JFP camp mention "political insider" clearly referencing that politicians have already endorsed Simotas.  I offered defense of these politicians, especially Dromm and Van Bramer.  I have also spoken highly of Maloney, Gianaris, and Quinn for the work they have done, and the respect they deserve for it.  I have said I thin it is unfair and a misnomer to consider Aravella a political insider because of support by these progressive politicians.  The real question is if her politics conform to the progressive democratic party's platform.  And they do.  If JFPs do also, then a new argument should be made by him. 

9.  I am ashamed that anyone would compare the discussions on this board with Karl Rove tactics.  That again smells of victimization talk rather than rational discussion.  It makes mountains out of mole-hills.  Additionally, one should really be thinking, that after one of the two wins the primary, they still have to win the election, and a divided democratic base would hurt either candidate.  Additionally, in the long run, we have to be a community afterwards.  Accusing anyone of of Karl Rove tactics seems a bit out of line.  It is like comparing someone to Hitler when they may have done a few rotten things in their life.  Hyperbole, and exaggeration.  It does not bring sympathy to a side, and is said to be inflammatory.  NEITHER SIDE has engaged thus far in tactics that warrant being called Karl Rove-esque.

Now that I've spent 25 minutes ranting, can we actually discuss the issues at hand? I'd love some answers to some of the questions posed to JFP's side.  I also want to be clear, that though I am a supporter of Simotas, I am not connected to her campaign.  And I speak without any prompting by them.  I believe what I believe because of what I've observed, in this race, observed in my friendships with both AS and JFP, and how I've sen both perform in civic and marriage equality-related associations.  All things tallied up, I'm supporting Simotas.

Quote

Jeremiah Frei-Pearson has worked primarily on the Oklahoma litigation and on monitoring reform in New Jersey and Washington, DC. Before joining Children’s Rights, Mr. Frei-Pearson practiced in the litigation department of Kaye Scholer LLP, where he worked on a variety of complex antitrust cases and pro bono matters. In 2004 and 2005, Mr. Frei-Pearson received the Kaye Scholer Pro Bono Achievement Award for his work on a death penalty case and several social security cases; he recently received the 2008 Thurgood Marshall Award from the New York City Bar Association for his pro bono death penalty work. He is currently a member of the New York State Bar Association’s Civil Rights Committee, an executive committee member of the American Constitution Society’s New York Lawyer Chapter, and a volunteer member of the Election Protection Coalition.

Mr. Frei-Pearson earned his B.A. (Phi Beta Kappa and magna cum laude) from Skidmore College in 2000, and his J.D. from Stanford Law School in 2003. As a law student, he was a Public Interest Fellow and Senior Symposium Editor of the Stanford Law & Policy Review. He organized and supervised a program providing direct legal services to poor people, taught children in prison, worked in a legal clinic for the mentally ill, and co-founded the Stanford Chapter of the American Constitution Society. In 2001, Mr. Frei-Pearson interned for the Honorable Shira Scheindlin of the Southern District of New York. As a college student, he interned for Senator Ted Kennedy and for several organizations that provide services to children.

From employer bio -



A life-long New Yorker, Aravella Simotas received her bachelor of arts degree, summa cum laude, from Fordham University in 1999 and her juris doctor degree from Fordham University School of Law in 2002. During law school, Ms. Simotas served as the managing editor of the Fordham Environmental Law Journal. She also worked as a district representative to the former Speaker of the New York City Council. An active community member, she has served on the Queens Community Board 1 since her May 2002 appointment by the Borough President.


Before joining Bickel & Brewer, Ms. Simotas clerked for Senior Judge Nicholas Tsoucalas and Judge Timothy C. Stanceu at the U.S. Court of International Trade (“CIT”). At the CIT, she focused on U.S. international trade law disputes between the United States and private parties. Such matters involved complex issues of administrative law. In addition, Ms. Simotas gained experience in a variety of civil and criminal matters during designation sittings at the Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit and the U.S. District Court for the Southern District of New York.

Ms. Simotas is admitted to practice in New York, New Jersey, the U.S. District Courts for the Southern District and Eastern District of New York, and the CIT.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mangopaco on May 04, 2010, 11:06:26 AM
As I do on my lunch breaks, I read up on national and local news while I eat.  Found this from two weeks ago that I missed:

http://www.queenstribune.com/not4pub/Not4pub_042210.html (http://www.queenstribune.com/not4pub/Not4pub_042210.html)

District 36

Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson, two bright, young, impressive candidates, are squaring off to replace Mike Gianaris in the Assembly – Gianaris will take George Onorato’s Senate seat with little or no opposition. Aravella, the insider in this race, with the endorsement of the present Assemblymember, appears to be using his influence to insure her election. She has all but been guaranteed the support of the Democratic Organization in the Primary.

But don’t count Jeremiah Frei-Pearson out. As a lawyer, Jeremiah has spent his career fighting to give voice to foster children and others who have been shut out and shoved aside by our political system.  He strongly believes that New York state government must work because our children need better schools, we all need quality healthcare, and we need a government that can tackle the serious economic problems we are facing. He is committed to working toward that end.

While Aravella places her priority as bringing home the bacon for the District, Jeremiah recognizes that Albany does not serve the people of his District or the State and places his priority at fixing the dysfunction in the State legislature.

It could be a classic battle of inside vs. outside. And while Aravella’s path of lining up the party’s support and promising to focus on fighting for the District’s share in Albany has been the typical path of victory in the Dem Primary, have the people reached their limit of Albany abuse and will they embrace Jeremiah’s vow to devote himself to changing Albany?

We’ll be watching.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mangopaco on May 12, 2010, 11:20:10 AM
Quote from: ddanny999 on May 11, 2010, 05:10:24 PM
If the United Food and Commercial Workers Union has placed their confidence and support for Aravella Simotas, I guess that's good enough for me.  The good people representing the United Food and Commercial Workers Union has never let me down.  The old Local 1500 wouldn't steer us wrong!

As a unionist (UFT), I agree that the union endorsements mean a lot.  If they have endorsed her, they obviously see the same good candidate that some have spoken about here.  However, it does not necessarily mean she's the best candidate.

As an active union member, I can attest to the politics involved in endorsements.  I have been a part of the endorsement process (not necessarily for the UFT) where the membership votes one way, but the Executive Board decides to go another way.  It happens in almost every union and advocacy group.  It has less to do with who will do the better job and more to do with who did the better politicking.  In this case, I can imagine how strong the lobbying is on Simotas' side on the part of Gianaris and his colleagues.  It probably makes the endorsement process a virtually one-sided affair.

So, like I said, a union's endorsement does go a long way and has been able to help inform my decisions in the past.  But, I encourage everyone to look beyond the endorsements and learn more about the candidates themselves. 

I agree with zippycar85 that I'd love to hear both candidates in a forum or debate.  That way you can decide for yourselves and not based on the politics of endorsement. 

Perhaps we can get an Astorians.com Candidates Forum going?  :?  A forum by the people and for the people.

Endorsements are nice but I base my vote on the candidate's record. Jeremiah has a proven record of fighting for the downtrodden and the hard-working people of our communities. As I've already said:

Quote from: mjmurphy on April 11, 2010, 10:44:13 PM
Jeremiah Frei-Pearson has the courage and integrity to be a true leader in a time when our government in New York is known more for scandal and corruption. He has a strong public record of fighting for the little guy. He works as an attorney for Children's Rights, where he helps get children out of broken foster systems into caring, safe, and healthy homes. He's well known in Astoria as part of the legal team who won a $63 million dollar settlement from ConEd to compensate the victims of the 2006 Queens Blackout and fund neighborhood Greening projects to improve the quality of life in our communities. Jeremiah rallied with the gay and lesbian community to fight for marriage rights and helped found Western Queens for Marriage Equality. He works with the Long Island City Alliance to keep poorly-planned development from disfiguring our neighborhoods.

Now Aravella Simotas apparently isn't happy with Jeremiah's good work for our neighborhoods. Simotas' spokesman attacked Jeremiah for his work fighting ConEd, claiming he "betrayed our community" because he didn't get enough out of ConEd. Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mjmurphy on May 13, 2010, 07:56:59 AM
Everything that transpired in the ConEd situation is a matter of public record.

Jeremiah and Western Queens Power for the People took ConEdison to court through a "prudence" proceeding via the public service commission. The settlement is publicly available at http://www.powerforthepeople.info/63millionproposal.html

It was signed by a variety of parties, including the Staff of the Department of Public Service, the New York State Consumer Protection Board, Western Queens Power for the People, New York Assemblyman Richard L. Brodsky, The City of New York, and the Public Utility Law Project.

The settlement did not prevent people from pursuing additional damages against ConEdison. What it did do was ensure that:

(1) ConEd apologized in writing (something they had refused to do at all, initially)
(2) Require ConEd to make restitution to everyone who lost money
(3) Ensure that the extent of the damages were documented
(4) Prevent ConEd from passing the cost on to rate payers
(5) Bring home money for greening projects to address the health concerns created by ConEd power plants in the area.

As for the many folks who suffered more than $100 in losses, State Law limits the maximum that ConEdison can pay. They actually brought home significantly more than most thought we were entitled to under state law (see this NY Times article saying ConEd was only liable for 9.3 million http://www.nytimes.com/2007/01/19/nyregion/19coned.html?_r=1).

The law needs to be updated to allow for greater reimbursement.  This hasn't happened because our broken government in Albany hasn't updated the reimbursement rates in over 30 years. In the Assembly, Jeremiah will fight to increase the reimbursement rate allowable.

Jeremiah Frei-Pearson stood with his neighbors and together, they fought to get what they could out of ConEd. Aravella Simotas did nothing and now she has the nerve to criticize Jeremiah for not doing enough.

As a member of that Astoria LGBT community, I always found myself somewhat suspicious of his motives, though I could very well be wrong.

And for what it's worth, I work in the child welfare field and among my colleagues, no one has a clue who he is, nor do I recall seeing him presenting at any professional conferences. Granted, while he would in all likelihood not have a clue who I am either, I probably wouldn't try to make my professional achievements seem like more than they are if I were running for office. It's a fairly small legal field. As for Simotas, I haven't a clue who she is, what she's done or what she stands for. I know she's gotten a number of endorsements, but that's about it.

If the only information a voter gets is from the two sides presented on the Astorians board from the warring factions, then I suspect a lot of voters might just stay home. The nitpicky fighting really doesn't help and certainly doesn't provide anyone with the tools to make an informed decision on election day.

Just my two cents.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: TRX on May 21, 2010, 04:51:50 PM
Quote from: mjmurphy on May 13, 2010, 07:56:59 AM
Everything that transpired in the ConEd situation is a matter of public record.

The settlement did not prevent people from pursuing additional damages against ConEdison. What it did do was ensure that:

(1) ConEd apologized in writing (something they had refused to do at all, initially)
(2) Require ConEd to make restitution to everyone who lost money
(3) Ensure that the extent of the damages were documented
(4) Prevent ConEd from passing the cost on to rate payers
(5) Bring home money for greening projects to address the health concerns created by ConEd power plants in the area.

As for the many folks who suffered more than $100 in losses, State Law limits the maximum that ConEdison can pay

I understand folks, repetition. There is a lot more to learn, but recognize facts.

If you were here, you know who was in the leadership then, and they dropped the ball big time.
Our local leadership supported the mayor who was patting the CEO of ConEd on the back.

You, I, and certainly Jeremiah would agree that the residents deserved a great deal more in compensation. I feel confident that if Jeremiah had been our Assembly member then, ConEd would have been howling even more. To say otherwise seems to show not having been involved much.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: hellsgatetim on May 21, 2010, 05:11:00 PM
I just got this from Simotas website

Aravella Simotas is a lifelong resident of Astoria with a strong commitment to her community and public service, and has devoted herself to making a positive impact on the lives of others.  Aravella’s career in public service began at the New York City Council’s Office of Oversight and Investigation, where she focused on various public safety, youth and environmental issues, and was followed by community affairs work at the offices of Council Members Peter Vallone, Sr. and Peter Vallone, Jr. Now, she is running for the State Assembly to continue delivering results for her community and middle-class families because she understands the serious issues facing western Queens.

A graduate of the New York City public school system, Aravella appreciates the value of a solid public education.  Aravella attended Public School 17, Junior High School 126 and William C. Bryant High School in Astoria, and continued her education at Fordham University and Fordham University School of Law.  Aravella is dedicated to ensuring that our children receive the same first-rate education that she did.  That’s why, as our next Assembly Member, Aravella will ensure that critical education funding is not cut during these tough economic times.

Aravella fully understands the environmental issues facing western Queens.  Over the years, Aravella has demonstrated a relentless commitment to our community’s environmental health.  While at the New York State Department of Environmental Conservation, Aravella advocated for environmental causes with New York State Assembly Member Michael Gianaris and fought to curb construction of highly polluting power plants.  Aravella’s hard work in this endeavor resulted in a reduction of over 250,000 pounds of our state’s annual toxic emissions.  In Albany, Aravella will continue her diligent environmental oversight so that western Queens remains a clean and safe place to live.

Aravella’s dedication to public service is rooted in her commitment to protecting the civil rights of all citizens.  Irrespective of one’s race, age, ethnicity, religion, gender, disability or sexual orientation, Aravella understands that equality for all should be the foundation of our society.  That’s why Aravella has volunteered a significant amount of her time to providing legal representation to the economically challenged, and has handled cases that have had a widespread impact on the local community.  Recently, Aravella was honored by the United Spinal Association for her part in representing an individual in a wheelchair who was denied access to his housing development and discriminated against on the basis of his disability.

Aravella is also a staunch supporter of LGBT rights.  Aravella knows that for too long, LGBT couples have been denied the rights and benefits they deserve, including social security benefits, hospital visitation rights, co-parenting rights, tax equity, and bi-national family-based immigration rights.   As our next Assembly Member, Aravella will fight to ensure that equality for all is finally enacted by our Legislature.

Aravella knows that working families are the cornerstone of New York’s economy.  As an attorney at the United States Court of International Trade, Aravella addressed disputes involving domestic companies and American workers who lost their jobs because of outsourcing.  In turn, these hardworking men and women received the benefits they deserved. In the Assembly, Aravella will continue to look out for working men and women and will fight to take away tax breaks for companies that outsource jobs overseas.

Aravella is a long serving member of Queens Community Board #1.  Aravella also serves on the boards of the United Community Civic Association and the Hellenic Times Scholarship Fund.  She was presented with a Citation of Honor by Queens Borough President Helen Marshall for her commitment to these and various other community organizations.  Aravella currently lives in Astoria with her husband John Katsanos.

Title: Regarding the ConEd issue
Post by: kempsternyc on May 23, 2010, 12:55:06 AM
The ConEd issue has been a confusing one for me.

The first question is who was/is Western Queens Power for the People. How did this organization come about? I've asked before and haven't received an answer.

The second is how the settlement came about. I just googled and came up with this link that contains a treasure trove of information from the Public Services Commission.

http://www3.dps.state.ny.us/W/PSCWeb.nsf/All/0F519E7284794F3085257687006F38D3?OpenDocument (http://www3.dps.state.ny.us/W/PSCWeb.nsf/All/0F519E7284794F3085257687006F38D3?OpenDocument)

There are two things that intrigued me as I clicked on the various links.

The first thing is that there was a final report released concerning the investigation into the power outage. It was released Feb 9th 2007 and is a 190 page document. So it isn't completely true that the settlement ended the investigation. But, interestingly, PCS wanted to continue the investigation. April 2007, they called for a Prudence Investigation that would, as far as I can tell, move from the factual investigation into more of an investigation of the culture/attitudes of ConED that would have created the process that would have lead to the blackout. I think that means looking into whether ConEd cared more about pleasing the shareholders then updating equipment.

Anyway, on April 24th 2008, a settlement was announced. And as you can see WQPFP wasn't the only group to sign off on it......Here's a link to a page that shows that four other groups signed off on it. http://www3.dps.state.ny.us/W/PSCWeb.nsf/All/ACD11A54EB8E5B7E85257696006D4A78?OpenDocument (http://www3.dps.state.ny.us/W/PSCWeb.nsf/All/ACD11A54EB8E5B7E85257696006D4A78?OpenDocument)

okay, now I just found an article from the Queens Gazette stating that state law actually doesn't allow for much more of a settlement.
http://qgazette.our-hometown.com/news/2008-04-30/Features/Lawmakers_Denounce_Con_Ed_For_Paltry_Blackout__Set.html (http://qgazette.our-hometown.com/news/2008-04-30/Features/Lawmakers_Denounce_Con_Ed_For_Paltry_Blackout__Set.html)

Here are two quotes
Quote
"This proposal must still be reviewed by the Public Service Commission before it goes into effect, and some have pointed out that we would not even be considering this settlement plan if it were not for the inadequacy of state laws that stymie efforts to hold private utilities truly accountable for their failures. No matter how this issue isultimately resolved, it is very clear that we need to make changes in our laws to better protect all of New York's communities from the type of devastation we experienced here in Queens."Vallone (D- Astoria) stated,

Quote
Alyssa Bonilla, of Sunnyside, a member of the Power for the People organization, stated: "The laws that currently exist to seek justice against a privately owned utility company are inadequate."

And to end this long post....Our retiring Sen Onorato had this to say.
Quote
"On the other hand, under the terms of this proposed settlement, Con Ed will not be able to pass along $40 million in outage related costs and $6 million in other charges to its customers, and it will provide $17 million from shareholder funds to pay for the refunds, community environmental projects, and a study on the economic and health impacts of the blackout. Members of the Western Queens Power for the People Campaign worked hard to win these concessions, and are to be commended for their efforts.

My conclusion:

An investigation was done and completed....but ConEd didn't want the prudence investigation.

The laws of our state didn't really provide for a more satisfactory settlement.

WQPFP worked hard to get terms beyond what the law allowed for.

And for all the carping by Maloney, Gianaris, Clinton et al........State Law Sucks.....and Western Queens Power For the People got us more that we actually would have gained.

ps....I just spent an hour creating this post because it is an important issue and not an attack on anyone...I do truly want to know what happened.

Chris Bragg, the author, calls it a sleepy race.  Has he not been on Astorians.com?  :-o



Conservative Democrat Enters Race For Gianaris Seat
By Chris Bragg

Add one more candidate to what at first seemed like it would be a sleepy race for the Assembly seat of Mike Gianaris.

John Ciafone, an attorney and former school board president in Western Queens is getting into the race—and he hopes to appeal to conservative Democrats with a platform which includes support for charter schools and opposing gay marriage.

Ciafone, who is Italian-American, officially announced his candidacy at a meeting Tuesday night the Long Island City-based Aldos Democratic Club, which he heads. The meeting was also attended by his two Democratic opponents in the race, civil rights attorney Jeremiah-Frei Pearson and corporate attorney Aravella Simotas.

Gianaris is running for the Senate seat being vacated by George Onorato, who is retiring.

Ciafone, who opposes same-sex marriage, said he would run to the right of the two other candidates, who are pro-same sex marriage and who so far have been jockeying for the liberal primary vote. The district has a heavy Latino, Greek, Irish and Eastern European populations that can be more socially conservative than the normal Democratic primary electorate. The district largely overlaps with that of Council Member Peter Vallone, Jr., one of the most conservative members of the City Council, and is squarely within the Senate district held by Onorato, who voted against the same-sex marriage bill.

Even though he is a former school board president in the area, Ciafone also said he was strongly in favor of lifting the charter school cap, which he said also said differentiates him from his two opponents.

“I saw first hand how afraid everyone was of the UFT,” he said. “Most politicians are afraid of them.”

Ciafone said he hopes charter school supporters will provide him funding in the race. He has hired consultant Michael Tobman, who is working with several pro-charter candidates this year.

Ciafone was complimentary of Frei-Pearson—whom Ciafone said had encouraged him to run—but bashed Simotas for her close ties to Gianaris and other members of the Queens Democratic Party, which last Monday voted to officially endorse Simotas.

“All the politicians have already gone with her,” Ciafone said. “They’re like the political mafia.”

As a conservative Democrat, Ciafone could cut into the base of older, more conservative voters in the area that typically back the county candidate, in this case Simotas. Frei-Pearson, meanwhile, is trying to make inroads with the younger voters that have moved into Astoria and Long Island City.

Simotas’ campaign, though, in a statement to City Hall said that, “It doesn’t matter who runs because Aravella is the best candidate and is going to win.”

That sentiment was echoed by Vallone, who beat Ciafone in a heated 2001 Council campaign. Vallone noted that Simotas, who is the first Greek-American woman to run for Assembly, already had lined up the support of the biggest Democratic club in the area, the Taminet Regular Democrat Club. Vallone has also personally endorsed Simotas.

“They’re the older voters who supported George Onorato for so many years,” Vallone said. “They have a very large membership, and they love Aravella.”

Gianaris is running for the Senate seat being vacated by George Onorato, who is retiring.

Ciafone, who opposes same-sex marriage, said he would run to the right of the two other candidates, who are pro-same sex marriage and who so far have been jockeying for the liberal primary vote. The district has a heavy Latino, Greek, Irish and Eastern European populations that can be more socially conservative than the normal Democratic primary electorate.


The district largely overlaps with that of Council Member Peter Vallone, Jr., one of the most conservative members of the City Council, and is squarely within the Senate district held by Onorato, who voted against the same-sex marriage bill.

Even though he is a former school board president in the area, Ciafone also said he was strongly in favor of lifting the charter school cap, which he said also said differentiates him from his two opponents.


“I saw first hand how afraid everyone was of the UFT,” he said. “Most politicians are afraid of them.”

Ciafone said he hopes charter school supporters will provide him funding in the race. He has hired consultant Michael Tobman, who is working with several pro-charter candidates this year.

Ciafone was complimentary of Frei-Pearson—whom Ciafone said had encouraged him to run—but bashed Simotas for her close ties to Gianaris and other members of the Queens Democratic Party, which last Monday voted to officially endorse Simotas.


“All the politicians have already gone with her,” Ciafone said. “They’re like the political mafia.”


As a conservative Democrat, Ciafone could cut into the base of older, more conservative voters in the area that typically back the county candidate, in this case Simotas. Frei-Pearson, meanwhile, is trying to make inroads with the younger voters that have moved into Astoria and Long Island City.

Simotas’ campaign, though, in a statement to City Hall said that, “It doesn’t matter who runs because Aravella is the best candidate and is going to win.”

That sentiment was echoed by Vallone, who beat Ciafone in a heated 2001 Council campaign, and has endorsed Simotas. Vallone noted that Simotas, who is the first Greek-American woman to run for Assembly, already had lined up the support of the biggest Democratic club in the area, the Taminet Regular Democrat Club.


“They’re the older voters who supported George Onorato for so many years,” Vallone said. “They have a very large membership, and they love Aravella.”

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: sting55 on May 28, 2010, 07:47:04 PM
New York Times

Violence Comes Uncomfortably Close to a Gay Shelter

By COLIN MOYNIHAN
Published: July 14, 2008
For the people who live at a residence for gay and transgender youth in Astoria, Queens, the cramped four-room apartment they share is a congenial harbor, a place where they do not have to worry about the prejudices and dangers they often face on the streets.
 
Ruby Washington/The New York Times

The Rev. Louis Braxton Jr.was attacked last week outside Carmen’s Place, a shelter he runs in Astoria, Queens.
Last Monday night those dangers arrived on their doorstep when a group of young people confronted the residents outside their home. Insults were exchanged and punches were thrown. No serious injuries resulted, but four teenagers were arrested and charged with using improvised weapons to attack an Episcopal priest who runs the shelter, which is called Carmen’s Place.

In the end, the confrontation could have been much worse, but the half-dozen or so residents of the shelter, who are in their late teens to mid-20s, said they were still alarmed.

“This is a safe haven for the kids,” said Michael Dropp, the president of the group’s board. “That’s why the things that happened Monday night are really a shame.”

That conflict began when the Rev. Louis Braxton Jr., who runs the shelter, witnessed teenagers striking a resident in the head with a bag of garbage. Moments later, Father Braxton said, the teenagers turned on him, striking him with an empty paint can, swinging metal shelf brackets at him and finally breaking a wooden miter box against his head. He was treated for minor injuries.

The police arrested four teenagers and charged them with assault, criminal possession of a weapon and harassment. Witnesses said that the teenagers shouted anti-gay slurs. The police were investigating whether the attack was motivated by bias. In the past few days, advocates and elected officials have condemned the attack.

A spokeswoman for the Legal Aid Society, which is representing one of the defendants, said the agency was looking into what happened.

Father Braxton said that he had called the police twice before for minor incidents, but that he had never experienced a conflict as serious as the one last week. Some Astoria residents who had heard about the attack expressed sympathy for the residents. Many others said that they had no idea that the residence existed.

Carmen’s Place opened in 2005 as part of St. Andrew’s Episcopal Church in Astoria, after Father Braxton allowed teenagers who had been living on neighborhood rooftops to sleep in the church basement.

After the church closed in 2007 because of financial difficulties, Father Braxton decided to continue the mission by renting a second-floor apartment on Steinway Street in Astoria, in the midst of a busy commercial strip.

There, anywhere from six to eight youths sleep in bunk beds and store their few possessions in metal lockers. There is always an adult chaperon on the premises. Carmen’s Place is the only residence in Queens for gay and transgender youths, and residents come from as far away as California and Hawaii.

Life is not always easy for Father Braxton’s flock. There are manipulative boyfriends to deal with and unfamiliar men who form odd obsessions after seeing residents on the streets. They are tempted by nighttime boulevards and alleys where sex can be sold as easily as cigarettes, Father Braxton said, and by an inclination to mistake the lust of strangers for romantic love. There is also harassment, running the gamut from nasty looks to rude words, or worse.

“I’ve been spit on,” said Cherry Snodgrass, a 20-year-old gay man from Oklahoma who lives at Carmen’s Place. “I’ve been hit.”

Some of residents battle depression or other disorders and take medication to stay on an even keel. Others have been ejected from similar shelters in Manhattan after behaving disruptively. For many of those who show up there, Carmen’s Place is a refuge of last resort, Father Braxton said.

Supervising the youths and trying to steer them toward productive paths can sometimes be difficult for Father Braxton, who said that he had served at parishes in Rye, N.Y., and Teaneck, N.J., before taking on the duties at St. Andrew’s. He said he was motivated by the urgency of trying to help people in need.

“The Gospel calls on us to feed the hungry and clothe the naked,” he said.

Fulfilling that charge is arduous. The residence relies on private donations and the largess of food pantries. Each week is a struggle to make ends meet, Father Braxton said.

One resident, Chloe Elsworth, 25, described coming to New York 18 months ago from Orange County, Calif., hoping to design clothes, but instead being kicked out of a Manhattan shelter and sleeping on the No. 2 train before being taken in at Carmen’s Place.

Ms. Elsworth said she was rattled when she saw Father Braxton being attacked.

“I was scared for him,” she said. “Seeing a man of the cloth being beat down like that was brutal.”

Father Braxton said he was planning to move to a bigger place with more security, provided he could raise the necessary money. He added that he had already chosen a spot — in the same neighborhood.

“Astoria people tend to mind their own business,” he said. “It tends to be a live-and-let-live kind of place.”

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mcdirk on May 29, 2010, 01:14:25 AM
Quote from: ditmarszoe on May 28, 2010, 05:11:06 PM
Thinking more about Vallone's comment. How can the LGBT community expect Simotas to really be a champion for marriage equality if she's depending on Onorato's supporters and can't afford to alienate them? Especially if she's competing with Ciafone for those voters!

I think this is an easy one to explain - many of the Onorato voters are older voters, Italians and Greeks, and many are active with the Taminent Regular Democratic Club, one of the most powerful clubs in Queens.  Many voters in this demographic are not quite there yet on LGBT issues, especially marriage, but people like Assemblymember Michael Gianaris, and candidate Aravella Simotas, have taken positions in support of equality and made some inroads in changing the way people think.  Aravella has known a lot of these people for her entire life and despite them disagreeing with her on marriage equality, I would imagine they will turn out to vote for her, knowing that she'll do a good job in representing the district in Albany. 

While marriage equality is a core issue for me as a gay man, and for many other newer residents to Astoria, it's not a core issue for many older voters - they may disagree on the issue, but it would not be enough to change their vote - I'd imagine sanitation, senior centers, development, health care and other quality of life issues are probably much greater determinants of their voting decisions.  Hope that helps.

BTW - I know folks are saying Ciafone jumping in hurts Simotas more than Frei-Pearson, but I'm not sure that's the case either.  The Aldos club voters do not generally vote for candidates out of the Taminent, though Aldos voters are more likely to support a Greek candidate.  I don't think they were going to vote for Aravella to begin with - they tend to go against the County organization and do their own thing, usually supporting insurgents more often than not.  I'm not convinced they were going for Jeremiah either though, it could be with Ciafone in the race, it just brings out voters who might not have pulled a lever in the Assembly race - I do doubt it is any sort of game-changer.
