LocalQueensCommunity Board 1 district manager George Delis hit with sex harass lawsuit     

Community Board 1 district manager George Delis hit with sex harass lawsuit
BY John Marzulli
DAILY NEWS STAFF WRITER

Tuesday, June 16th 2009, 10:07 PM
 
George Delis known as the "mayor of Astoria," retired in 2008 after 30 years as the district manager.A former female staffer at Community Board 1 in Astoria is alleging she was sexually harassed by longtime district manager George Delis, according to explosive charges in a lawsuit.

Marcela Gutierrez contends in the suit that she was forced to quit her job as a receptionist in December 2007 because her complaints about Delis' behavior were ignored by board Chairman Vinicio Donato and, as a result, her health was deteriorating.

Gutierrez alleges that Delis frequently made comments about his sexual prowess, twice invited her to watch pornographic films in his office, openly touched his private parts and referred to her as a "hooker" and a "lesbian," according to the suit filed in Brooklyn Federal Court.

Delis, 64, a charismatic community activist who is known as the "mayor of Astoria," retired in 2008 after 30 years as the district manager.

The suit also alleges that Delis was thrown under the bus by Donato in sworn testimony before an unemployment insurance appeal board.

"Mr. Donato testified that 'On many occasions, [Gutierrez] had come to me complaining about [Delis'] abusive language to her and reference to her sexual preference,'" according to the complaint.

The suit seeks unspecified monetary damages from Delis, Donato, the City of New York and Queens Borough President Helen Marshall, who appoints the district managers and has a supervisory function over the boards.

Marshall's spokesman said the borough president's office has no record of complaints filed by Gutierrez.

Donato refused to comment, but Delis had plenty to say about the suit.

"I had nothing but problems with her," Delis told the Daily News.

"She was totally incompetent. She bragged about being gay, and she hit on every woman who came in the office. Why would I watch adult movies with her? I couldn't stand her."  
Donato hired Gutierrez for the $24,000-a-year job without going through the proper screening by the board because she was his daughter's baby-sitter, Delis said.

"Vinny should step down before this gets messy, because I'm not a guy who backs off," Delis said.

Gutierrez's lawyer said yesterday he had nothing to say beyond what is stated in the suit.

The city Law Department said yesterday it is reviewing the case "thoroughly."


Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: sting55 on May 29, 2010, 05:52:18 AM
City settles federal sexual harassment suit against George Delis for $98,000
BY John Marzulli
DAILY NEWS STAFF WRITER

Thursday, March 4th 2010, 4:00 AM
 
George Delis was accused of sexual harrassment by a female staffer. The city has paid a $98,000 settlement to a former female staffer at Community Board 1 in Astoria who had claimed in a federal lawsuit that she was sexually harassed by former Board 1 district manager George Delis.

Marcela Gutierrez's explosive allegations included Delis inviting her to watch pornographic films in his office, commenting about the size of her breasts and constantly bragging about his sexual conquests.

Gutierrez also claimed that Delis referred to her as a "hooker" and a "lesbian."
The suit, filed last June in Brooklyn Federal Court, also named Queens Borough President Helen Marshall and the board's chairman, Vinicio Donato, as defendants for failing to control Delis.

A spokeswoman for the city Law Department said the settlement was in the best interest of all parties - but Delis and his lawyer blasted the payout.

"I objected to settling," Delis told the Daily News. "It was all a crock of s--t. The fact that she's getting anything is an injustice."

"She was incompetent and the lawsuit was retaliation because I told her to get out or I'd write her up and get her fired," Delis added.

Gutierrez claimed she quit her $24,000-a-year job as an aide due to Delis' alleged abuse. Her lawyer, Bruce Bernstein of New Jersey, said they were satisfied with the settlement and declined further comment.

Delis, who retired in 2008 and is known as the "mayor of Astoria," said he favored fighting the charges all the way to a trial.

"Though the city opted to settle, there was no finding or admission of any wrongdoing by Mr. Delis," said Walter Kretz, an attorney hired by the city to represent Delis.

Assemblyman Michael Gianaris (D-Astoria) said it was unfortunate taxpayers had to foot the bill for Delis' alleged behavior. "He [Delis] should have to reimburse the city for the damages," Gianaris said.

jmarzulli@nydailynews.com

I think this is an easy one to explain - many of the Onorato voters are older voters, Italians and Greeks, and many are active with the Taminent Regular Democratic Club, one of the most powerful clubs in Queens.  Many voters in this demographic are not quite there yet on LGBT issues, especially marriage, but people like Assemblymember Michael Gianaris, and candidate Aravella Simotas, have taken positions in support of equality and made some inroads in changing the way people think.  Aravella has known a lot of these people for her entire life and despite them disagreeing with her on marriage equality, I would imagine they will turn out to vote for her, knowing that she'll do a good job in representing the district in Albany.

I think mcdirk's analysis is correct and true.

I do not believe John Ciafone will be a factor in the race, because like Jeremiah Frei-Pearson, he does not have sufficient name recognition among voters.  Older Italian and Greek voters will gravitate to Aravella Simotas even though many are not aware of current issues in Albany or the candidates core competencies.  Those that do attend the political clubs can intelligently discuss issues and candidates and they do influence their family and friends on whom to vote for.

The question is, is the newer influx of residents and progressives formidable enough to overcome the status-quo?  Last year, Lynn Serpe got 22% of votes in the city council election.  Not bad considering that she had no endorsements from the local political clubs or newspapers, limited name recognition and a modest warchest compared to Peter Vallone.

Aravella Simotas is being groomed for this election by the establishment and likely to win, but there is room for an upset.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: sting55 on May 29, 2010, 06:24:27 AM
City Hall News

Conservative Democrat Enters Race For Gianaris Seat
By Chris Bragg
 
Add one more candidate to what at first seemed like it would be a sleepy race for the Assembly seat of Mike Gianaris.


John Ciafone, an attorney and former school board president in Western Queens is getting into the race—and he hopes to appeal to conservative Democrats with a platform which includes support for charter schools and opposing gay marriage.

Ciafone, who is Italian-American, officially announced his candidacy at a meeting Tuesday night the Long Island City-based Aldos Democratic Club, which he heads. The meeting was also attended by his two Democratic opponents in the race, civil rights attorney Jeremiah-Frei Pearson and corporate attorney Aravella Simotas.


Gianaris is running for the Senate seat being vacated by George Onorato, who is retiring.

Ciafone, who opposes same-sex marriage, said he would run to the right of the two other candidates, who are pro-same sex marriage and who so far have been jockeying for the liberal primary vote. The district has a heavy Latino, Greek, Irish and Eastern European populations that can be more socially conservative than the normal Democratic primary electorate.


The district largely overlaps with that of Council Member Peter Vallone, Jr., one of the most conservative members of the City Council, and is squarely within the Senate district held by Onorato, who voted against the same-sex marriage bill.

Even though he is a former school board president in the area, Ciafone also said he was strongly in favor of lifting the charter school cap, which he said also said differentiates him from his two opponents.


“I saw first hand how afraid everyone was of the UFT,” he said. “Most politicians are afraid of them.”

Ciafone said he hopes charter school supporters will provide him funding in the race. He has hired consultant Michael Tobman, who is working with several pro-charter candidates this year.

Ciafone was complimentary of Frei-Pearson—whom Ciafone said had encouraged him to run—but bashed Simotas for her close ties to Gianaris and other members of the Queens Democratic Party, which last Monday voted to officially endorse Simotas.


“All the politicians have already gone with her,” Ciafone said. “They’re like the political mafia.”


As a conservative Democrat, Ciafone could cut into the base of older, more conservative voters in the area that typically back the county candidate, in this case Simotas. Frei-Pearson, meanwhile, is trying to make inroads with the younger voters that have moved into Astoria and Long Island City.

Simotas’ campaign, though, in a statement to City Hall said that, “It doesn’t matter who runs because Aravella is the best candidate and is going to win.”

That sentiment was echoed by Vallone, who beat Ciafone in a heated 2001 Council campaign, and has endorsed Simotas. Vallone noted that Simotas, who is the first Greek-American woman to run for Assembly, already had lined up the support of the biggest Democratic club in the area, the Taminet Regular Democrat Club.


“They’re the older voters who supported George Onorato for so many years,” Vallone said. “They have a very large membership, and they love Aravella.”

Astoria's representatives, Mike Gianaris and George Onorato, just voted to cut $775 million dollars from New York's healthcare; taking away indigent care funding for people who can't afford insurance and reducing Medicaid reimbursements for the poor. How can we expect their protege, Simotas, to do any different? I think that's the fundamental question of her candidacy: she's a product of the same Albany system that gives us scandal, corruption, and failure. How on earth is can we expect her to be anything but more of the same?

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion

holyfrjole, the Party has proved fairly resilient in adapting to challengers--once they win. Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mjmurphy on June 14, 2010, 04:11:10 PM
For the folks that have been saying how they'd like to hear more from the candidates, I have good news! Jeremiah invited his opponents to 9 debates in a letter sent to each campaign today by his Campaign Manager.

Here's the text of the letter:

In exactly three months, the people of our community will decide who will represent them in the State Assembly. It’s the first time in a decade that this district will not have an incumbent in the running, which makes this election a unique chance for the voters to choose a new direction for our government. With government dysfunction leaving our community in the lurch day after day, the stakes are high. Jeremiah Frei-Pearson feels that the candidates owe the people of our community every opportunity to hear from those who seek to represent them.
 
Political debates are a time-honored tradition that will give the voters a forum to hear the candidates discuss and defend their visions for our community. Jeremiah believes that a robust contest of ideas strengthens our democracy and helps ensure that our neighbors will make an informed decision on September 14th. With that in mind, he issues this challenge: Aravella Simotas and John Ciafone meet Jeremiah for nine debates, open to the public, before election day. We suggest each candidate choose a debate venue in the order in which they announced their candidacies. This will ensure a fair process and a diverse set of forums.
 
I’m certain the three campaigns can come to an agreement on matters such as times, dates, and other specifics. In the interests of scheduling, however, I ask that you please confirm your acceptance of this proposal by Wednesday, June 16th and that the first venue be chosen by Friday, June 18th.
 
In three months, our neighbors will choose from three individuals offering three different paths for our community. Let’s give them the chance to make the most informed choice possible.
 
Sincerely,
 
Jesse Laymon
Campaign Manager
Jeremiah Frei-Pearson for Assembly

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: hellsgatetim on June 14, 2010, 05:30:26 PM
Quote from: mjmurphy on June 14, 2010, 04:11:10 PM
For the folks that have been saying how they'd like to hear more from the candidates, I have good news! Jeremiah invited his opponents to 9 debates in a letter sent to each campaign today by his Campaign Manager.

Here's the text of the letter:

In exactly three months, the people of our community will decide who will represent them in the State Assembly. It’s the first time in a decade that this district will not have an incumbent in the running, which makes this election a unique chance for the voters to choose a new direction for our government. With government dysfunction leaving our community in the lurch day after day, the stakes are high. Jeremiah Frei-Pearson feels that the candidates owe the people of our community every opportunity to hear from those who seek to represent them.
 
Political debates are a time-honored tradition that will give the voters a forum to hear the candidates discuss and defend their visions for our community. Jeremiah believes that a robust contest of ideas strengthens our democracy and helps ensure that our neighbors will make an informed decision on September 14th. With that in mind, he issues this challenge: Aravella Simotas and John Ciafone meet Jeremiah for nine debates, open to the public, before election day. We suggest each candidate choose a debate venue in the order in which they announced their candidacies. This will ensure a fair process and a diverse set of forums.
 
I’m certain the three campaigns can come to an agreement on matters such as times, dates, and other specifics. In the interests of scheduling, however, I ask that you please confirm your acceptance of this proposal by Wednesday, June 16th and that the first venue be chosen by Friday, June 18th.
 
In three months, our neighbors will choose from three individuals offering three different paths for our community. Let’s give them the chance to make the most informed choice possible.
 
Sincerely,
 
Jesse Laymon
Campaign Manager
Jeremiah Frei-Pearson for Assembly

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mjmurphy on June 25, 2010, 05:12:40 PM
Talk about clearing the air.

Anyway, a lot of folks on this board have asked for more specifics from the candidates. So here are two policy statements Jeremiah has made which weren't picked up by the press, so you probably didn't know about.

Sensible Zoning:

"The Zoning Proposal coming before City Council today is the result of eight years of hard work carried out by the people of our communities. I've been proud to stand with them and stand up to over-development that distorts the character of our neighborhoods and puts unsustainable stress on our infrastructure. Over a year ago, as a member of the Long Island City Alliance, I called for rezoning to protect and preserve the unique character of our neighborhoods and the quality of life in our communities. I am very proud to see this process finally come to a vote in our City Council.

But this is only the beginning. More needs to be done to ensure that our subways, our electrical grid, our schools, and our hospitals can handle our growing population. Many times, I've joined my neighbors to rally and speak out against over-development. Recently, I have helped gather signatures to prevent tenement-style construction near Athens Square Park that would over-stress our resources, contribute to over-crowding, and reduce the quality of life in our area. Time and time again, we've shown that when people come together as a community, we can enact real change. And that is what we need to bring to Albany now. In the Assembly, I will continue to stand with the people of our neighborhoods to bring change to Albany and fight to keep over-development from disfiguring and overwhelming our communities."

Living Wages:

"I strongly support the Fair Wages for New Yorkers Act. It is unconscionable that any working people live in poverty in a city that has more billionaires than any other place on earth. The working families of New York deserve better. This bill is an important first step to securing the foundation of our economy: the hard-working men and women of our communities.

When I'm elected to our Assembly, I pledge to introduce a similar bill to protect the middle and working class people of our State. By guaranteeing them the fair wage they deserve, we will provide much-needed security to the people who drive our economy and we will invest in sustainable, bottom-up growth that will strengthen and rebuild our State."

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: holyfrjole on June 29, 2010, 12:37:37 PM
After reviewing the positions and qualifications of both candidates, I am pro-Simotas. I am not a troll, don't work for her campaign, and have engaged in discussions on this board that have nothing to do with politics.

Simotas and Frei-Pearson have very similar positions on the issues that are important to me. Where they differ is their background. Aravella is a lifelong Astoria resident with strong ties to the community. As a lifelong Astoria resident myself, I respect that and believe that she can appreciate both the new, younger generation moving into Astoria as a less expensive alternative to Manhattan and Brooklyn, as well as the old Astoria residents who laid down roots here decades ago.

I firmly believe it's important for both Astorias to be represented -- the old and the new -- and think that Aravella can do that. While I'm sure JFP would do just as good of a job if elected, I think Aravella would be more responsive to the needs of the community based upon her strong ties and roots here.

While I do believe that JFP has laid down roots in this neighborhood and I greatly appreciate what he has done in the time he's been here, I just don't believe he has the same insight into the community that she does.

In reality, endorsements don't typically influence my vote, but in this situation, people who I respect have thrown their support her way and I can appreciate that. Had they endorsed JFP, I would have considered the reasons why as well.

The "change" and "more of the same" argument may have worked for Barack Obama's campaign in 2008, but it's really not applicable here. Mike Gianaris did a great job as Assemblyman and quite frankly, if we can expect "more of the same" of that from Aravella, I'd be perfectly happy. The status quo in Albany can be blamed on senators like Ruben Diaz and Pedro Espada and assembly members like Sheldon Silver. Onorato represented this neighborhood for so long, he became completely out of touch with it. Fortunately Onorato will be replaced by Gianaris, so at least one creaky cog in the wheel will be gone. I suspect that Aravella has been "hand picked" because she's capable, intelligent, respected, and will do an excellent job representing this community.

And fwiw, check out her Facebook page and you'll see where she's been. I haven't seen JFP anywhere, does that mean he hasn't been out there? No. I don't profess to be everywhere at all times, I can't imagine you are either.

Well, first of all I can't imagine that one can get through law school and not be intelligent -- I've been to law school, it's not exactly easy. I imagine that she's respected because she's earned the support of many other well-respected people. I have no evidence that JFP is intelligent, respected and will do a good job either -- but I suspect that he is, and would do a good job as well. I don't think it's an especially difficult conclusion to come to about either candidate.

Second, she says she supports gay marriage. I don't believe one needed to protest at Onorato's office to prove that. I support gay marriage and I wasn't at Onorato's protesting either. JFP took that particular issue and ran with it -- I appreciate that, believe me, I do -- but to me, there's more to life in Astoria than marriage equality.

I'm not a single issue voter. I don't think someone earns my vote just because they've "[fought] for the LGBT citizens of Astoria." It's nice that there are candidates out there that support the LGBT community and recognize the importance of equality, but being gay is not the be all end all of who I am. I'd rather see a politician that works to get our neighborhood better access to education and better funding for social service programs. If they support equality, even better.

Someone asked if there was anyone here who supported her who didn't work for her campaign -- I responded. Why you feel the need to aggressively challenge me about my choice seems kind of odd. I get that you're a JFP supporter, but I would think that a respectful dialogue about why we support our candidates would go much further to make one's point.

Title: Re: Aravella Simotas and Jeremiah Frei-Pearson Discussion
Post by: mjmurphy on July 19, 2010, 08:21:52 AM
Here is Jeremiah's statement on the decision to end the race:

Quote
Together, we collected a massive number of signatures and raised more money than all but one non-incumbent Assembly candidate in Queens. More importantly, we helped frame the terms of this debate. We lead the fight for marriage equality, for good government, better schools, more hospitals, a sane energy policy, and a government that doesn't ignore the 80,000 children in Queens who live in poverty. I am very proud of our what we accomplished and of the values we fought for.
 
Unfortunately, the dynamics of the race have changed in the past week. After this past week's developments, we still have path to victory - but that path would require us to run a negative campaign against a fellow Democrat.  This is a path that I am unwilling to take.
 
As a result, after many discussions and lots of prayer, Karla and I have decided not to go forward with this campaign. This was a very tough decision - and it was made even more difficult by the amazing outpouring of support we received.
 
Although this political campaign is ending, the causes for which we fight endure. I am looking forward to working with Marriage Equality New York to help all New Yorkers get the right to marry; I am looking forward to continuing to fight to ensure that more children get the opportunities they need; so that our community's schools improve, so that we get more hospital beds, so that immigrants are welcome throughout our country, and so that we can finally fix our energy policy. We have lots of work to do and I hope you will continue to work alongside me.

Of course I'm saddened by this decision. But even so, I understand and support Jeremiah's reasons for ending the campaign. His only remaining path to victory required a negative campaign against a Democrat with a considerable following in the District. He's put our community and our shared values ahead of this single election and I can assure all of you that he isn't going anywhere. We will continue to have his leadership, his support, and his advocacy on all the important issues facing our communities.

I strongly believe that competitive primaries are good for our Party and good for the people. A robust contest allows the best candidates to emerge, vetted out in the open by the people. I believe that we've achieved that for Astoria. We know a lot more about all the candidates and their views than we would've if Jeremiah hadn't made his bid. There are 36 pages of discussion on this forum that never would've happened if Jeremiah hadn't run. This race has also proven that Aravella Simotas has tremendous support in our community. I've had the opportunity to speak with her on several occasions and I have found her to be intelligent, interested, and open to good ideas from wherever they emerge. She will be Astoria's voice in our Assembly and I hope we can all come together to work with her on the issues facing our community.

I take stabs at the Astoria Political Machine for its evident entitlement, obsequious self-praise (on this message board and in print), and for positioning a woman for the Assembly whose greatest accomplishment, frankly, is being Greek.  However, Aravella's campaign is effective and she communicated better than Jeremiah.

Here is how Aravella described herself on her campaign website (first paragraph bio): "Aravella Simotas is a lifelong resident of Astoria with a strong commitment to her community and public service, and has devoted herself to making a positive impact on the lives of others."

Here is how Jeremiah described himself on his campaign website (first paragraph bio): "Jeremiah Frei-Pearson lives in Astoria with his wife, Karla Mosley Frei-Pearson, and their two cats: Scooby and Scrappy."

This is not a contrast of style, this is a WTF gaffe.

Jeremiah is grassroots and organic, while Aravella is establishment and systemic.  She has an enormous warchest (with a billionaire organizing her fundraisers), political connections, advisors and endorsers at her side, and a local newspaper that celebrates her every move.

I guess Aravella's supporters are relieved since there is no other candidate to stand in her way (and John Ciafone doesn't count).  They can breathlessly swoon over Aravella as she is "changing the way Albany does business" ...for the next twenty years.
